# sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/#sunc-documentation)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/README.md "View source of this page")

sUNC Documentation
==================

Welcome to the official documentation for **sUNC** - senS' Unified Naming Convention.

This documentation site serves as the central knowledge base for understanding what sUNC is, how it works, and how to contribute to the project.

Whether you're an executor developer, a curious tester, or a contributor helping document functions, you're in the right place!

Not every original UNC function is tested!

This documentation covers **_only_** the functions that are **actively tested by the sUNC script**. If a function is not listed here, then it is likely not part of our standard.

Over time, sUNC has largely diverged from the original UNC to become better and shaped by executor developers and users, hence why some functions have been deprecated/removed and others may have been added.

* * *

📚 Explore the Docs
-------------------

*   [What is sUNC?](https://docs.sunc.su/About/what-is-sunc/)
    
*   [How sUNC Test Results Work](https://docs.sunc.su/About/test-results/)
    
*   [How to contribute](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/)
    

📜 The script
-------------

| The sUNC testing script |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-1)<br>[2](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-2)<br>[3](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-3)<br>[4](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-4)<br>[5](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-5)<br>[6](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-6)<br>[7](https://docs.sunc.su/#__codelineno-0-7) | `getgenv().sUNCDebug = {     ["printcheckpoints"] = false,    ["delaybetweentests"] = 0,    ["printtesttimetaken"] = false, } loadstring(game:HttpGet("https://script.sunc.su/"))() -- (1)` |

1.  This loadstring uses [script.sunc.su](https://script.sunc.su/)
    , which is an official mirror of the sUNC script. If the mirror is down or you would like to use the original loadstring, visit [this](https://gitlab.com/sens3/nebunu/-/raw/main/HummingBird8's_sUNC_yes_i_moved_to_gitlab_because_my_github_acc_got_brickedd/sUNCm0m3n7.lua)
    .

Please note that as of sUNC v2.0, the test now only runs inside of the official testing game. The latest one may be retrieved from [our Discord server](https://discord.gg/FNNfTUpFYv)
.

* * *

Thank you for being here.

Back to top

# Contribution Guide - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#contribution-guide)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/contributing.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/contributing.md "View source of this page")

Contribution Guide
==================

Welcome to the sUNC documentation project! We worked tirelessly to standardise and make the documentation beautiful and readable for everyone.

This guide outlines the official standards for contributing to the sUNC documentation, including how libraries and functions should be structured and written.

Consistency makes the documentation readable, searchable, and enjoyable to explore.

* * *

Documenting entire libraries
----------------------------

Each library **must** be placed in a folder named after the library itself. Inside this folder, you must include a `README.md` file, which serves as the **index page** for that library, in both this documentation website and also when browsing the documentation repository on GitHub.

### Index page requirements

*   Introduce the purpose of the library
*   Summarise what you **can** and **cannot** do with it

Index pages _do not_ need to follow this strict format, but they should **_aim_** to do so, for clarity and helpfulness.

* * *

General documentation style
---------------------------

All documentation pages (including function pages and index pages) **must**:

*   Use inline links to relevant [Wikipedia](https://wikipedia.org/)
    , [Roblox Luau](https://create.roblox.com/docs)
    , or other sUNC pages with referencing key terms.
*   Use the correct inline link formats, e.g.:
    
    ``[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-0-1) [`#!luau task.defer`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/libraries/task#defer)``
    
    As you can see, the example above uses a code snippet with `luau` syntax highlighting enabled, whilst also being a hyperlink to the Roblox API documentation for [`task.defer`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/libraries/task#defer)
    .
    

All markdown documents must be formatted using David Anson's ["markdownlint"](https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=DavidAnson.vscode-markdownlint)
 extension, available for free in the Visual Studio marketplace.

This extension alone is not sufficient enough, which is why we use Yu Zhang's ["markdown all in one"](https://marketplace.visualstudio.com/items?itemName=yzhang.markdown-all-in-one)
 extension too, but only specifically for formatting tables. This makes tables look nice and readable in the source markdown files of the documentation.

The repository for this documentation already includes a `.vscode/extensions.json` file, so the extensions should automatically download for you once you consent.

When formatting tables, open the Command Palette with `Ctrl + Shift + P` (Windows) or `⌘ + Shift + P` (macOS), select "Format Document With...", and select "Markdown All In One" like so:

![Formatting a markdown document using the Markdown All In One extension in Visual Studio Code](https://docs.sunc.su/About/assets/markdown-formatting.gif)

### Language choices

#### Using British English

It is generally well known around the sUNC community that the documentation and most things that have a lot of text are written using British English. This usually means some words Americans spell with a "z" will instead use an "s". If you are unsure, please check the Oxford or Cambridge dictionaries.

#### The "Oxford Comma"

Please use the [Oxford Comma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serial_comma)
 when writing lists.  
This means that in a list of three or more items, a comma is placed before the final "and" or "or".  
For example: _"apples, oranges, and bananas"_ rather than _"apples, oranges and bananas"_.

The Oxford Comma avoids ambiguity and makes lists clearer. It also mirrors natural pauses in daily speech, which makes the text easier to read aloud and less confusing to follow.

#### Short-form contractions

Please avoid contractions like "isn't" and "it's". Instead, use "is not" and "it is" respectively. These are just examples, but the same rules apply for all contractions. Because this documentation is formal and technical rather than conversational, contractions should be avoided.

#### Articles before a word

An article is something that goes before a word, like `a` and `an`. This is a polite reminder to **_not_** just put an `an` in front of things that have a vowel _literally_, but rather whether the word has a vowel **sound** when pronounced out loud. Non-native English speakers tend to get this rule wrong sometimes.

If unsure about pronunciation, assume that pronunciation is done with a British RP accent - the best sources to listen to are the Oxford and Cambridge dictionaries again where the pronunciation is perfect.

* * *

Function documentation
----------------------

Each function must have **its own file**, named after the function (e.g. `newcclosure.md`).

### Title Format

The title of the page must be written as:

`` [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-1-1) # `function_name` ``

Important

Do not include emojis in function **titles**.

### Notices

Place all important `!!!` callouts (warnings, errors, info) **immediately under the title**. These should include anything the user must know before using the function.

* * *

### Description

Provide a description of the function directly after any notices.

When referencing the function name, **always** use the code snippet format:

``[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-2-1) `#!luau function_name` allows you to do this and that.``

* * *

### Type definition

Type definitions are important!

You **must** always include a Luau-style type definition when documenting a function.

Include the Luau type definition **at the bottom of the first section**, with Luau syntax highlighting but **no _individual line highlighting_ or line numbers**:

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-3-1) function newcclosure<A..., R...>(functionToWrap: (A...) -> R...): (A...) -> R...`

Make sure it precedes the parameters table.

* * *

### Parameters

The parameters must always be neatly described in a function, like so:

``[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-4-1) ## Parameters [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-4-2)[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-4-3) | Parameter               | Description                         | [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-4-4) |-------------------------|-------------------------------------| [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-4-5) | `#!luau parameter_name` | Short description of the parameter. |``

Use [**snake\_case**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snake_case)
 for **every variable**, and [**camelCase**](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camel_case)
 for **parameters** to easily distinguish between the two.

There should be **no horizontal rule** (`---`) between the _type definition_ and the _parameters_ section.

* * *

### Providing users with examples

Every function page **must** include at least one example.

Use 'Example' or 'Examples' based on how many examples you have

To make the documentation experience more logical and also grammatically correct, please do the following: - Make the heading `## Example` if there is only one example. - Make the heading `## Examples` if there is more than one example. Each example should have its own subheading, e.g. `### Example 1`, `### Example 2`.

Each example should use the following format:

` [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-1) ## Example [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-2)[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-3) ```luau title="Short but descriptive title for your code" linenums="1" [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-4) -- an example is here [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-5) print("Hello world!") [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-6) print("This is some example code") [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/contributing/#__codelineno-5-7) ``` `

*   Examples must use `luau` syntax highlighting.
*   Line numbers **must** be enabled using `linenums="1"`.
*   Each example **must** have a `title` describing in short what the code does.

Back to top

---

# How do test results work? - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/test-results/#how-do-test-results-work)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/test-results.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/test-results.md "View source of this page")

How do test results work?
=========================

sUNC is known for its strict tests. Ever since it was made, it was built to expose falsified environments and spoofed globaly by testing for functionality - not just checking for their presence or shallow checking.

* * *

Using the dedicated game
------------------------

As of **sUNC V2**, all tests must be conducted in the official sUNC testing game. This game may be found in our [Discord server](https://discord.gg/FNNfTUpFYv)
.

We chose to do so, because by having a dedicated server, we're able to provide you with the new online test results via Rubiš. This allows us to provide you with verified and reproducible results, instead of people sending meaningless screenshots of their console output.

* * *

Viewing your test results
-------------------------

Once your test is complete, sUNC will generate a short redirect link via `r.sunc.su` like this:

![An r.sunc.su redirect link generated](https://docs.sunc.su/About/assets/test-results/r.sunc.su.png)

This generated link redirects to **Numelon Rubiš**:

![An sUNC Test Result being displayed with Numelon Rubiš](https://docs.sunc.su/About/assets/test-results/RubisTestResult.png)

The results page offers a clean, visually appealing UI that lays out which functions passed and which failed, why they failed, and cryptographic guarantees of authenticity.

* * *

Verified integrity
------------------

Rubiš doesn't just store your sUNC test results, it also **verifies** them.

*   Every result is **cryptographically signed** by the sUNC test game servers.
*   Any tampered or faked data is **flagged as unverified**.

Even if someone tries to replicate the link or manually upload fake data and use it with the results viewer (since [Rubiš is also a public paste service](https://rubis.app/)
 which is usable by anyone), it will not work.

Back to top

---

# sUNC introduction - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/what-is-sunc/#sunc-introduction)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/what-is-sunc.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/what-is-sunc.md "View source of this page")

sUNC introduction
=================

What is "sUNC"?
---------------

**sUNC** stands for **senS' Unified Naming Convention**. It is a tool designed to check if an executor can properly run essential global functions, following the existing [Unified Naming Convention](https://github.com/unified-naming-convention/NamingStandard/tree/main)
.

Unlike the original UNC (which is now outdated and prone to spoofing), sUNC ensures that functions actually work as intended, by testing them as if they were to be used in a real scenario. However, we are not in any way calling UNC "bad". We are simply stating that people should not be using UNC to deeply test their environment, as it was never intended to do so.

How would I know what fails?
----------------------------

We are not gatekeeping function tests, despite the script being obfuscated.  
You are welcome to ask the owner (@sens6222 on Discord) **if you are struggling with passing certain tests**. We keep it this way for now, due to executors already faking their environments to suit the original UNC.

Note that it's also possible to see the detailed reason of a function's failure at the top of the `Developer Console` in game, or on the dedicated sUNC Rubiš site.

Will sUNC be discontinued?
--------------------------

Not in the near future, we hope. However, if sUNC were to be discontinued, we will open source the project after 1-2 months.

* * *

Credits
-------

*   [Original UNC Documentation](https://github.com/unified-naming-convention/NamingStandard/tree/main)
    

Back to top

---

# sUNC Integration Suite - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/#sunc-integration-suite)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/README.md "View source of this page")

sUNC Integration Suite
======================

This integration suite is not related to the functions outlined in the rest of the documentation; this is a **WEB DEVELOPMENT** thing.

The **sUNC Integration Suite** provides a set of external-facing tools and APIs that allow developers to embed sUNC into their own websites, dashboards, or infrastructure.

This suite is especially useful for web developers who work on status websites, people who want to show off their test score on their exploit website, or forums where embedding is allowed.

* * *

What can you do?
----------------

With the sUNC Integration Suite, you can:

*   **Embed** rich test result viewers into your site using the [**widget system**](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/)
    
*   **Fetch** live, structured function metadata using the [**sUNC Metadata API**](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/)
    

* * *

Support
-------

If you require some assistance or would like some new features in any part of the sUNC Integration Suite, e.g. the widget system, please do not hesitate to contact [`@iirzd`](https://richy.lol/)
 in the [sUNC Discord server](https://discord.gg/FNNfTUpFYv)
.

Back to top

---

# postMessage - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#postmessage)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/README.md "View source of this page")

`postMessage`
=============

`postMessage` sends a typed message to a sUNC Widget `<iframe>`, allowing you to dynamically interact with the widget by sending messages from your host page.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-1) type SuncWidgetMessage =   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-2)   | {    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-3)     type: "sunc-widget:loadScrap";    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-4)     payload: {      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-5)       scrapId: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-6)       key: string;    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-7)     };  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-8)   }  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-9)   | {    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-10)     type: "sunc-widget:setTheme";    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-11)     payload: {      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-12)       dark?: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-13)       light?: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-14)       lighter?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-15)      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-16)       sunc?: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-17)       suncLighter?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-18)      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-19)       grey?: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-20)       lightText?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-21)      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-22)       success?: string;      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-23)       failure?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-24)      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-25)       useDarkLogo?: boolean;    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-26)     };  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-27)   }; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-28)[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/#__codelineno-0-29) function postMessage(message: SuncWidgetMessage, targetOrigin: string): void;`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `message` | The structured [message](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/)<br> to send to the sUNC widget. |
| `targetOrigin` | The expected origin of the iframe, which should always be `"https://sunc.rubis.app"`. |

* * *

Notes
-----

*   `targetOrigin` **must exactly match** the origin of the `<iframe>` source to avoid your message being ignored - this should always be `"https://sunc.rubis.app"`.
*   The widget ignores unknown or malformed message types.
*   Missing theme properties in `sunc-widget:setTheme` will fall back to the default sUNC colour palette.

Back to top

---

# Closures - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/#closures)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/README.md "View source of this page")

Closures
========

The **Closures** library enables the inspection, modification and creation of Luau closures with precise control.

It is one of the most powerful tools available, exposing internals in a way that Luau does not natively support out of the box.

This library is incredibly useful for hooking functions to modify game logic to your own advantage, and any other creative uses you can think of.

* * *

What is a closure?
------------------

The term [_"closure"_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Closure_(computer_programming))
 comes from [functional programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Functional_programming)
 and refers to a function **_plus_** the environment it carries (its **upvalues**).

In Luau, **every function is implemented as a closure** implicitly, even if it doesn't capture anything.

* * *

What can you do?
----------------

With the `Closures` library, you can:

*   **Hook** existing functions or metamethods with [`hookfunction`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/)
     and [`hookmetamethod`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/)
    
*   **Check** whether the current execution is from your script using [`checkcaller`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/)
     for **hooking**
*   **Clone** a function while keeping the same behavior to avoid tampering, with [`clonefunction`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/)
    
*   **Wrap** a Luau closure into a C closure using [`newcclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/)
    
*   **Check** a function's closure type with [`iscclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/iscclosure/)
    , [`islclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/)
     or [`isexecutorclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/)
    .
*   **Hash** a function with [`getfunctionhash`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/)
    

* * *

What can't you do?
------------------

Although closure capabilities are powerful, there are natural boundaries:

*   You cannot inspect **true C closures' internals** - they are not Luau-defined, compiled, and therefore opaque by design.
*   Attempting to implement [`newcclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/)
     in Luau (e.g. via [`coroutine.wrap`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/libraries/coroutine#wrap)
    ) **will fail sUNC verification**.

Back to top

---

# checkcaller - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#checkcaller)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/checkcaller.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/checkcaller.md "View source of this page")

`checkcaller`
=============

`checkcaller` returns a boolean indicating whether the **current function was invoked from the executor's own thread**. This is useful for differentiating between your own calls and those made by the game.

It is often used in [`hookfunction`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/)
 and/or [`hookmetamethod`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/)
.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-0-1) function checkcaller(): boolean`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| _(none)_ | This function takes no parameters. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Identifying the source of a \_\_namecall |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-14)<br>[15](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/checkcaller/#__codelineno-1-15) | `local from_caller local original; original = hookmetamethod(game, "__namecall", function(...)     if not from_caller then        from_caller = checkcaller()    end     return original(...) end) task.wait(0.1) -- Step a bit hookmetamethod(game, "__namecall", original) print(from_caller)       -- Output: false print(checkcaller())    -- Output: true (current thread)` |

Back to top

# clonefunction - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#clonefunction)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/clonefunction.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/clonefunction.md "View source of this page")

`clonefunction`
===============

Notes on `clonefunction`

The new (cloned) function returned by `clonefunction` should have the same environment as the original function.

Any sort of modification to the original function **should not** affect the clone. This means that stuff like hooking the original function will leave the clone **unaffected**.

`clonefunction` creates and returns a new function that has the exact same behaviour as the passed function.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-0-1) function clonefunction<A..., R...>(functionToClone: (A...) -> R...): (A...) -> R...`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `functionToClone` | The function to clone. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Cloning functions with clonefunction |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/clonefunction/#__codelineno-1-10) | `local function dummy_function()     print("Hello") end local cloned_function = clonefunction(dummy_function) print(debug.info(cloned_function, "l")) -- Output: 1 print(debug.info(cloned_function, "n")) -- Output: dummy_function print(cloned_function == dummy_function) -- Output: false print(getfenv(cloned_function) == getfenv(dummy_function)) -- Output: true` |

Back to top

# Widget API Message Types - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#widget-api-message-types)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType.md "View source of this page")

Widget API Message Types
========================

`sunc-widget:loadScrap`
-----------------------

Loads a test result from the provided `scrapId` and `accessKey`.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-0-1) type LoadScrapPayload = {   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-0-2)   scrapId: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-0-3)   key: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-0-4) };`

### Parameters

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `scrapId` | The unique ID of the test result. |
| `key` | The access key required to view the test. |

### Example

| Load a test result |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-1)<br>[2](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-2)<br>[3](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-3)<br>[4](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-4)<br>[5](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-5)<br>[6](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-6)<br>[7](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-1-7) | `iframe.contentWindow.postMessage({   type: "sunc-widget:loadScrap",  payload: {    scrapId: "abc123XYZ",    key: "someAccessKey"  } }, "https://sunc.rubis.app");` |

* * *

`sunc-widget:setTheme`
----------------------

Updates the colour theme of the widget to match your branding. Any missing fields will fall back to defaults.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-1) type ThemePayload = {   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-2)   dark?: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-3)   light?: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-4)   lighter?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-5)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-6)   sunc?: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-7)   suncLighter?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-8)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-9)   grey?: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-10)   lightText?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-11)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-12)   success?: string;  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-13)   failure?: string; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-14)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-15)   useDarkLogo?: boolean; [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-2-16) };`

### Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Description | Default |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `dark` | `string` | Primary background colour for the entire widget. | `#12121c` |
| `light` | `string` | The secondary colour used for function cards and the summary on the right. | `#1b1b2a` |
| `lighter` | `string` | Colour used for the information bar at the top. | `#1c1b28` |
| `sunc` | `string` | Brand accent colour to be used by the info text, circle stroke and passed amount. | `#b7a0f6` |
| `suncLighter` | `string` | Used for hover effects, like the Numelon link at the bottom. | `#d1b9ff` |
| `grey` | `string` | Used for muted UI elements like search input icons, placeholder text, and metadata titles in the summary area. | `#aaaaaa` |
| `lightText` | `string` | Main readable text colour - used in the widget "Test Result" title, percentage label inside ring, and metadata values in the summary area and button text. | `#e0e0e0` |
| `success` | `string` | Colour used to indicate passed tests. | `#22c55e` |
| `failure` | `string` | Colour used for general failures, notably in the list of functions but also for widget errors and the "x tests failed" text. | `#ef4444` |
| `useDarkLogo` | `string` | Whether to use a light-friendly (dark) version of the sUNC logo. Set to `false` if you are using a light theme. | `true` |

### Clarification on colour names

You may have noticed that the colour names (like `dark`, `light`, `lighter`) do not follow typical design conventions like `primary`/`secondary`/`tertiary`. In hindsight, they might seem a bit misleading at first glance - however they are named based on **where they are used** in the widget, not their strict visual roles.

The image below visually presents parts of the SEW with the colour names they are associated with - and the names start to make much more sense. For example, `dark` corresponds to the deepest background colour in the very background of the page, `light` is the colour of the main title bar at the top where the sUNC logo, and `lighter` is literally a slightly lighter colour for the information bar below the title bar, et cetera:

![Visual overview of the colours for the sUNC Embeddable Widget](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/assets/SEW-colours.jpg)

### Logo Comparison

The sUNC logo shown in the top left of the widget can be customised depending on whether you intend to use a light theme or a dark theme. This is important to get right, otherwise you will have horrible contrast in the title bar of the widget.

If `useDarkLogo` is omitted entirely, then the widget defaults to `true` - it uses the dark logo by default.

#### `useDarkLogo: false`

When `useDarkLogo` is set to `false`, a light variant is used. This is perfect for when the background is dark as it provides enough contrast.

**Use this when you have a dark theme.**

![sUNC Full Light Logo](https://sunc.su/sunc-full.png)

#### `useDarkLogo: true`

When `useDarkLogo` is set to `true`, a dark variant is used. This is perfect for when the background is light as it provides enough contrast.

**Use this when you have a light theme.**

![sUNC Full Light Logo](https://sunc.su/sunc-full-dark.png?useNew)

### Examples

#### Example 3

Preview of the Default theme

Not Initialised ![sUNC Widget Default Theme, Not Initialised](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/assets/default-notinit.jpg)

Spoofed ![sUNC Widget Default Theme, Spoofed](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/assets/default-spoofed.jpg)

Result ![sUNC Widget Default Theme, Result](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/assets/default-result.jpg) 

| Applying a dark, electric yellow theme |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-5-1)<br>[2](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-5-2)<br>[3](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-5-3)<br>[4](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-5-4)<br>[5](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/#__codelineno-5-5) | `iframe.contentWindow.postMessage({     type: "sunc-widget:setTheme",     payload: {} // (1) }, "https://sunc.rubis.app");` |

1.  To revert back to the default theme, one may simply pass a message with an empty payload using the `postMessage` API.

# getfunctionhash - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#getfunctionhash)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/getfunctionhash.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/getfunctionhash.md "View source of this page")

`getfunctionhash`
=================

`getfunctionhash` returns the **_hex-represented_** [SHA384 hash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SHA-2)
 of a provided function's instructions (code) and constants.

C closures are not supported

This function will throw an error if called on a C closure, such as [`print`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/globals/LuaGlobals#print)
, since C closures have no reliable information to hash. The error should be something along the lines of `lua function expected`

Notes on `getfunctionhash`

In order to have reliable knowledge over what the function changes, `constants` should **also** be added to the hash alongside the `l.p->code`. Add the constants at the beginning of the instructions, and hash that.

We suggest following [this implementation](https://rubis.app/view?scrap=mwDweOS6zirsPJtc&type=cpp)
 in order to keep the same functionality across multiple executors, since it will be more convenient for the users not having to change their hashes if they do migrate to a different executor.

Full credits go to Dottik and Ragnar regarding the source provided above.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-0-1) function getfunctionhash(functionToHash: (...any) -> (...any)): string`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `functionToHash` | The function to retrieve the hash of. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Checking the SHA384 hash of functions with getfunctionhash |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/getfunctionhash/#__codelineno-1-14) | `local function is_sha384_hex(hash)     return #hash == 96 and hash:match("^[0-9a-fA-F]+$") ~= nil end local dummy_function_0 = function() end local dummy_function_1 = function(...) end local dummy_function_2 = function() end local dummy_function_3 = function() return "Constant" end local dummy_function_4 = function() return "Constant2" end print(is_sha384_hex(getfunctionhash(dummy_function_0))) -- Output: true print(getfunctionhash(dummy_function_0) == getfunctionhash(dummy_function_1)) -- Output: false print(getfunctionhash(dummy_function_0) == getfunctionhash(dummy_function_2)) -- Output: true print(getfunctionhash(dummy_function_3) == getfunctionhash(dummy_function_4)) -- Output: false` |

Back to top

# Widget - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#widget)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/README.md "View source of this page")

The sUNC Embeddable Widget (SEW) allows you to embed sUNC test results as interactive widgets into other webpages via an `<iframe>`. The widget is reusable and highly customiseable using it's [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
.

This widget is ideal for developers who want to display sUNC results on status websites, show their score off on an executor website, or to use it in forums.

* * *

Widget features
---------------

*   Load any sUNC test result into a sandboxed viewer widget.
*   Change the widget theme to match your website using a custom colour scheme.
*   Dynamically control the widget through JavaScript using the [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
    .

* * *

Example
-------

![sUNC Widget Example](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/assets/widget.gif)

You may view this example preview [here](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/example/)
 or look at the [source code](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/example)
.

* * *

Usage
-----

You can embed the widget using a standard `<iframe>` and control it using the [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
.

A minimum height of `610px` is **recommended**, but not required.

Embedding the sUNC widget

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-0-1) <iframe id="sunc-widget" src="https://sunc.rubis.app/widget/" allowfullscreen></iframe>`

Sending a message to load a scrap (test result)

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-1) <script>   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-2)   const iframe = document.getElementById("sunc-widget"); [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-3)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-4)   iframe.contentWindow.postMessage({    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-5)     type: "sunc-widget:loadScrap",    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-6)     payload: {      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-7)       scrapId: "766F7uirM9D9ZlAF",      [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-8)       key: "Hvj2XFk6nVJtJQQ9VtPoHoDpnxBDhesL"    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-9)     }  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-10)   }, "https://sunc.rubis.app"); [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-1-11) </script>`

Communicating with the widget may be done via the [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
, and [message types are described here](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/MessageType/)
.

* * *

Optimisation Guide: A Persistent SEW
------------------------------------

A minimum height of `610px` is **recommended**, but not required.

If your site frequently uses the sUNC Embeddable Widget (SEW) - for example, to display many different results or support multiple themes (e.g., an executor comparison website) - then it is **highly recommended** that you **keep a persistent `<iframe>`** in the DOM rather than dynamically creating and destroying it. In fact, the SEW was designed around this principle and is easier to use this way.

Instead of doing something like this:

The bad practice of dynamically creating a new iframe each time

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-1) // do NOT do this!! [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-2) button.onclick = () => {   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-3)   const iframe = document.createElement("iframe")  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-4)   iframe.src = "https://sunc.rubis.app/widget/"  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-5)   document.body.appendChild(iframe) [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-6)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-7)   iframe.contentWindow.postMessage({ ... }, "https://sunc.rubis.app") [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-2-8) }`

You should **ensure that the `<iframe>` exists only once** - whether this is dynamically created or _already present_ in your HTML - and keep it hidden by default (e.g., with Tailwind's `hidden` class or `display: none` in CSS). Then simply show, hide, or update it as needed:

Creating one persistent widget with the name of 'sunc-widget'

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-3-1) <iframe id="sunc-widget" class="hidden" src="https://sunc.rubis.app/widget/"></iframe>`

Then use the [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
 to load different results or change the theme:

Using the postMessage API to load a different result

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-1) iframe.contentWindow.postMessage({   [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-2)   type: "sunc-widget:loadScrap", [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-3)  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-4)   payload: {    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-5)     scrapId: "...",    [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-6)     key: "..."  [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-7)   } [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/#__codelineno-4-8) }, "https://sunc.rubis.app");`

### Why is this better?

Overall, using a persistent `<iframe>` is better because of a few reasons:

1.  Even if the widget might be cached by the browser, it does not need to re-initialise the `<iframe>` every time.
2.  Performance is slightly improved by avoiding unnecessary DOM churn and repeated `<iframe>` creation.
3.  Your state is perserved in the widget, meaning you can set a custom theme once and it will persist across result reloads.
4.  If your site supports multiple themes (e.g., light/dark mode, seasonal themes like a halloween theme for example), then you can instantly update the widget using the [`postMessage` API](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Widget/postMessage-API/)
     without waiting for the SEW to re-load, or having to maintain a separate state in your own code just to provide the SEW with your custom theme.

Back to top

---

# Metadata API - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#metadata-api)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/README.md "View source of this page")

Metadata API
============

The **sUNC Metadata API (SMA)** provides machine-friendly JSON datasets containing metadata for every documented sUNC function and library.

This API is designed for integration into apps, extensions, custom documentation browsers, or anywhere you want access to sUNC data programmatically. For example, we use the mini version in our test results viewer and the jumbo version for our Discord bot, sunc-chan.

**You can access it [here](https://docs.sunc.su/api)
.**

* * *

Versions
--------

You can choose between two formats depending on your needs.

### Mini Version (~10KB)

A lightweight object which maps function names to their descriptions.

* * *

### Jumbo Version (~45KB)

A fully structured, enriched metadata dump including:

*   Function signatures
*   Parameter names and descriptions
*   Type information
*   Library overviews
*   Direct links to the official documentation

* * *

Format
------

Both versions are served as `application/json` and are **automatically kept in sync** with the official sUNC documentation. You do not need an API key or authentication to use this API.

* * *

Example Usage
-------------

Fetching the mini version to print clonefunction's description

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#__codelineno-0-1) const res = await fetch("https://docs.sunc.su/api/mini.json"); [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#__codelineno-0-2) const metadata = await res.json(); [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#__codelineno-0-3)[](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#__codelineno-0-4) console.log(metadata["clonefunction"]); [](https://docs.sunc.su/About/Integration-Suite/Metadata-API/#__codelineno-0-5) // Output: "clonefunction creates and returns a new function that has the exact same behaviour as the passed function."`

Back to top

---

# hookfunction - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#hookfunction)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/hookfunction.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/hookfunction.md "View source of this page")

`hookfunction`
==============

Notes on `hookfunction`

The hook should not have more upvalues than the function you want to hook. There are ways to bypass the upvalue restriction, such as using `newlclosure` or [`newcclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/)
 to wrap the `hook`

All possible hooking closure pairs should be supported throughout L, NC, C (where NC = [`newcclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/)
)

`hookfunction` allows you to hook a function with another wanted function, returning the original unhooked function.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-0-1) function hookfunction<A1..., R1..., A2..., R2...>(functionToHook: (A1...) -> R1..., hook: (A2...) -> R2...): (A1...) -> R1...`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `functionToHook` | The function that will be hooked |
| `hook` | The function that will be used as a hook |

* * *

Example
-------

| Hooking functions with hookfunction |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/#__codelineno-1-14) | `local function dummy_func()     print("I am not hooked!") end local function dummy_hook()     print("I am hooked!") end dummy_func() -- Output: I am not hooked! local old_func = hookfunction(dummy_func, dummy_hook) dummy_func() -- Output: I am hooked! old_func() -- Output: I am not hooked!` |

Back to top

---

# hookmetamethod - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#hookmetamethod)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/hookmetamethod.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/hookmetamethod.md "View source of this page")

`hookmetamethod`
================

Notes on `hookmetamethod`

`hookmetamethod` can be safely implemented from within Luau, **as long as [`hookfunction`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/)
 is already properly implemented in C++**.

`hookmetamethod` takes any Luau object that can have a metatable, and attempts to hook the specified metamethod of the object. Internally, it essentially uses [`hookfunction`](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookfunction/)
 to hook specific metamethods.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-0-1) function hookmetamethod(object: { [any]: any } | Instance | userdata, metamethodName: string, hook: (...any) -> (...any)): (...any) -> (...any)`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `object` | The object which has a metatable. |
| `metamethodName` | The name of the metamethod to hook. |
| `hook` | The function that will be used as a hook. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Easily hooking metamethods with hookmetamethod |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-1)<br>[2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-2)<br>[3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-3)<br>[4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-4)<br>[5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-5)<br>[6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-6)<br>[7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-7)<br>[8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-8)<br>[9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/hookmetamethod/#__codelineno-1-9) | `local original; original = hookmetamethod(game, "__index", function(...)     local key = select(2, ...)    print(key)    return original(...) end) local _ = game.PlaceId -- Output: "PlaceId" hookmetamethod(game, "__index", original) -- Restores game's __index` |

Back to top

| --- | --- |

# Debug - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/#debug)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Debug/README.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Debug/README.md "View source of this page")

Debug
=====

The **Debug** library offers powerful tools for inspecting and modifying Luau functions at a bytecode level.

It allows you to access constants, upvalues, stack frames, and internal structures of functions that would otherwise be hidden - making it especially useful for reverse engineering and hooking.

* * *

What can you do?
----------------

With the Debug library, you can:

*   **Inspect** constants with [`debug.getconstants`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/)
    , [`debug.getconstant`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstant/)
    
*   **Modify** constants using [`debug.setconstant`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/setconstant/)
    
*   **Access** upvalues using [`debug.getupvalues`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getupvalues/)
     and [`debug.getupvalue`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getupvalue/)
    
*   **Replace** upvalues with [`debug.setupvalue`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/setupvalue/)
    
*   **Read** or **write** values from a stack frame, using [`debug.getstack`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/)
     and [`debug.setstack`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/setstack/)
    
*   **List** or **retrieve** function prototypes, using [`debug.getprotos`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/)
     and [`debug.getproto`](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getproto/)
    

* * *

What can't you do?
------------------

*   You cannot access C closures with this library, such as [`print`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/globals/LuaGlobals#print)
    

Back to top

---

# islclosure - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#islclosure)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/islclosure.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/islclosure.md "View source of this page")

`islclosure`
============

`islclosure` checks whether a given function is a Luau closure or not.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-0-1) function islclosure(func: (...any) -> (...any)): boolean`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `func` | The function to check. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Verifying Luau closures with islclosure |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/islclosure/#__codelineno-1-13) | `local function dummy_lua_function()     print("This is an executor Luau closure") end local dummy_cfunction = newcclosure(function()     print("This is an executor C closure") end) local dummy_standard_cfunction = print print(islclosure(dummy_lua_function)) -- Output: true print(islclosure(dummy_standard_cfunction)) -- Output: false print(islclosure(dummy_cfunction)) -- Output: false` |

# restorefunction - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#restorefunction)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/restorefunction.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/restorefunction.md "View source of this page")

`restorefunction`
=================

This will throw an error if the requested function is not already hooked

`restorefunction` restores a hooked function back to the very first original function, even if it has been hooked multiple times.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-0-1) function restorefunction(functionToRestore: (...any) -> (...any)): ()`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `functionToRestore` | The hooked function that you want to restore |

* * *

Examples
--------

### Example 1

| Restoring a hooked function |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-1-11) | `function dummy_func()     print("I am not hooked!") end hookfunction(dummy_func, function()     print("I am hooked!") end) dummy_func() -- Output: I am hooked! restorefunction(dummy_func) dummy_func() -- Output: I am not hooked!` |

### Example 2

| Restoring a unhooked function |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-1)<br>[2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-2)<br>[3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-3)<br>[4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-4)<br>[5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-5)<br>[6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/restorefunction/#__codelineno-2-6) | `function dummy_func()     print("I am not hooked!") end dummy_func() -- Output: I am not hooked! restorefunction(dummy_func) -- Error: restorefunction: function is not hooked` |

`isexecutorclosure`
===================

`isexecutorclosure` checks whether a given function is a closure of the executor. This also includes closures retrieved using [`getscriptclosure`](https://docs.sunc.su/Scripts/getloadedmodules/)
 or [`loadstring`](https://docs.sunc.su/Scripts/loadstring/)

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-0-1) function isexecutorclosure(func: (...any) -> (...any)): boolean`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `func` | The function to check. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Identifying executor closures with isexecutorclosure |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-14)<br>[15](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/isexecutorclosure/#__codelineno-1-15) | `local function dummy_lua_function()     print("This is an executor Luau closure") end local dummy_cfunction = newcclosure(function()     print("This is an executor C closure") end) local dummy_standard_cfunction = print local dummy_global_cfunction = getgc print(isexecutorclosure(dummy_lua_function)) -- Output: true print(isexecutorclosure(dummy_cfunction)) -- Output: true print(isexecutorclosure(dummy_global_cfunction)) -- Output: true print(isexecutorclosure(dummy_standard_cfunction)) -- Output: false` |

# newcclosure - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#newcclosure)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Closures/newcclosure.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Closures/newcclosure.md "View source of this page")

`newcclosure`
=============

Do not implement this with coroutines

Many executors seem to be implementing this function using [`coroutine`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/libraries/coroutine)
 functions in Luau. Such functions **will not pass sUNC checks**.

The wrapped function **must** be yieldable, meaning that the function should be able to call [`task.wait`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/libraries/task#wait)
, for example.

Error spoofing

Luau and C errors are different. You must ensure that errors from functions wrapped with `newcclosure` appear as C closure errors!

Upvalues

The function returned by `newcclosure` must have no upvalues.

`newcclosure` takes any Luau function and wraps it into a C closure. When the returned function is called, it invokes the original Luau closure with the provided arguments, then passes the closure's returned values back to the caller.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-0-1) function newcclosure<A..., R...>(functionToWrap: (A...) -> R...): (A...) -> R...`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `functionToWrap` | A function to be wrapped. |

* * *

Examples
--------

### Example 1

| Basic C closure wrapping example with newcclosure |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-1-12) | `local dummy_function = function(...)     return ... end print(iscclosure(dummy_function)) -- Output: false local wrapped_function = newcclosure(dummy_function) print(iscclosure(wrapped_function)) -- Output: true local function_results = wrapped_function("Hello") print(function_results) -- Output: Hello` |

### Example 2

This example illustrates how Luau functions wrapped as a C closure should also be yieldable, therefore also showcasing how coroutine implementations of `newcclosure` would not work.

| Yieldable C functions made with newcclosure |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Closures/newcclosure/#__codelineno-2-11) | `local dummy_yielding_function = newcclosure(function()     print("Before")    task.wait(1.5)    print("After") end) dummy_yielding_function() -- Output: -- Before -- yield for 1.5 seconds -- After` |

Back to top

# debug.getstack - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#debuggetstack)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Debug/getstack.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Debug/getstack.md "View source of this page")

`debug.getstack`
================

C closures are not supported

This function will throw an error if the stack level points to a C closure, such as `getstack(0)`.

`debug.getstack` retrieves values from the stack at the specified call level.

This function is useful for inspecting local variables or arguments at different layers of the stack frame. If no index is given, all values at that stack level are returned as a list.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-0-1) function debug.getstack(level: number, index: number?): any | { any }`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `level` | The stack level to inspect. `1` is the current function. |
| `index?` | The specific slot/index at that stack level to read. |

* * *

Examples
--------

### Example 1

| Retrieving multiple values from the stack |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-14)<br>[15](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-15)<br>[16](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-16)<br>[17](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-17)<br>[18](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-18)<br>[19](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-19)<br>[20](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-20)<br>[21](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-21)<br>[22](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-22)<br>[23](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-23)<br>[24](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-24)<br>[25](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-1-25) | `local count = 0 local function recursive_function()     count += 1    if count > 6 then return end     local a = 29    local b = true    local c = "Example"    a += 1    b = false    c ..= "s"     print(debug.getstack(1, count))    recursive_function() end recursive_function() -- Output (varies depending on Count): -- 30 -- false -- Examples -- function: 0x... (print) -- function: 0x... (getstack) -- etc.` |

### Example 2

| Retrieving values from the caller's stack |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getstack/#__codelineno-2-11) | `local function dummy_function()     return "Hello" end local var = 5 var += 1 (function()     print(debug.getstack(2)[1]()) -- Output: Hello    print(debug.getstack(2)[2])   -- Output: 6 end)()` |

# debug.getprotos - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#debuggetprotos)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Debug/getprotos.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Debug/getprotos.md "View source of this page")

`debug.getprotos`
=================

C closures are not supported

This function will throw an error if called on a C closure, such as [`print`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/globals/LuaGlobals#print)
, since C closures do not contain function prototypes.

Inactive protos

Protos retrieved without the `activated` should not be callable; this leads to vulnerabilities. The usage of inactive protos is to retrieve information off of them.

`debug.getprotos` returns all function prototypes defined within the specified Luau function.

These are internal function definitions (e.g. nested functions) that exist as part of the compiled bytecode, even if they aren't assigned or called.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-0-1) function debug.getprotos(func: (...any) -> (...any) | number): { (...any) -> (...any) }`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `func` | The Luau function (or stack level) to extract protos from. |

* * *

Example
-------

| Getting nested function prototypes |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getprotos/#__codelineno-1-12) | `local function DummyFunction0()     local function DummyFunction1() end    local function DummyFunction2() end end for index, proto in pairs(debug.getprotos(DummyFunction0)) do     print(index, debug.info(proto, "n")) end -- Output: -- 1 DummyFunction1 -- 2 DummyFunction2` |

Back to top

---

# debug.getconstants - sUNC Documentation

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#debuggetconstants)

[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/edit/main/docs/Debug/getconstants.md "Edit this page")
[](https://github.com/sUNC-Utilities/docs.sunc.su/raw/main/docs/Debug/getconstants.md "View source of this page")

`debug.getconstants`
====================

C closures are not supported

This function will throw an error if called on a C closure, such as [`print`](https://create.roblox.com/docs/reference/engine/globals/LuaGlobals#print)
, since C closures have no accessible constants.

`debug.getconstants` returns a list of all constants used within a Luau function's bytecode. This includes literal values like numbers, strings, booleans, and `nil`.

`[](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-0-1) function debug.getconstants(func: (...any) -> (...any) | number): { number | string | boolean | nil }`

Parameters
----------

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `func` | The Luau function (or stack level) whose constants will be returned. |

* * *

Examples
--------

### Example 1

| Retrieving constants from a Luau function |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-1)<br> [2](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-2)<br> [3](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-3)<br> [4](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-4)<br> [5](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-5)<br> [6](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-6)<br> [7](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-7)<br> [8](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-8)<br> [9](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-9)<br>[10](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-10)<br>[11](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-11)<br>[12](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-12)<br>[13](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-13)<br>[14](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-14)<br>[15](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-1-15) | ``local function dummy_function()     local dummy_string = "foo bar"    string.split(dummy_string, " ") end local constants = debug.getconstants(dummy_function) for constant_index, constant in constants do     print(`[{constant_index}]: {constant}`) end -- Output: -- [1]: "string" -- [2]: "split" -- [4]: "foo bar" -- [5]: " "`` |

### Example 2

| Calling on a C closure should error |     |
| --- | --- |
| [1](https://docs.sunc.su/Debug/getconstants/#__codelineno-2-1) | `print(debug.getconstants(print)) -- Should error due to being a C closure` |

Back to top
